Tonantzintla, 72840 Puebla, Mexico)"], "journal_name": "The Astrophysical Journal", "volume": "838", "publication_year": "2017/04/1", "start_page": "137", "keywords": ["galaxies: evolution", "galaxies: high-redshift", "galaxies: star formation", "gravitational lensing: strong", "infrared: galaxies", "dust", "extinction", "Astrophysics - Astrophysics of Galaxies", "Astrophysics - Cosmology and Nongalactic Astrophysics"], "url": "https://ui.adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2017ApJ...838..137P", "abstract": "We directly detect dust emission in an optically detected, multiply imaged galaxy lensed by the Frontier Fields cluster MACSJ0717.5+3745. We detect two images of the same galaxy at 1.1 mm with the AzTEC camera on the Large Millimeter Telescope leaving no ambiguity in the counterpart identification. This galaxy, MACS0717_Az9, is at z > 4 and the strong lensing model (\u03bc = 7.5) allows us to calculate an intrinsic IR luminosity of 9.7 \u00d7 10<SUP>10</SUP> L <SUB>\u2299</SUB> and an obscured star formation rate of 14.6 \u00b1 4.5 M <SUB>\u2299</SUB> yr<SUP>-1</SUP>. The unobscured star formation rate from the UV is only 4.1 \u00b1 0.3 M <SUB>\u2299</SUB> yr<SUP>-1</SUP>, which means the total star formation rate (18.7 \u00b1 4.5 M <SUB>\u2299</SUB> yr<SUP>-1</SUP>) is dominated (75%-80%) by the obscured component. With an intrinsic stellar mass of only 6.9 \u00d7 10<SUP>9</SUP> M <SUB>\u2299</SUB>, MACS0717_Az9 is one of only a handful of z > 4 galaxies at these lower masses that is detected in dust emission. This galaxy lies close to the estimated star formation sequence at this epoch. However, it does not lie on the dust obscuration relation (IRX-\u03b2) for local starburst galaxies and is instead consistent with the Small Magellanic Cloud attenuation law. This remarkable lower mass galaxy, showing signs of both low metallicity and high dust content, may challenge our picture of dust production in the early universe.", "doi": "10.3847/1538-4357/aa6573", <div class=\"overlay-text\">\n            <p>The American Astronomical Society (AAS), established in 1899 and based in Washington, DC, is the major organization of professional astronomers in North America. Its membership of about 7,000 individuals also includes physicists, mathematicians, geologists, engineers, and others whose research and educational interests lie within the broad spectrum of subjects comprising contemporary astronomy. The mission of the AAS is to enhance and share humanity's scientific understanding of the universe.</p> <p><a href=\"https://aas.org/\">https://aas.org/</a></div>\n        <p class=\"ta-c mt-1 mb-2\"><a href=\"\"></a></p>\n    </div>\n</span>\n<!-- Partner logo tile ends -->\n\n<!-- Partner logo tile starts -->\n<a href=\"\" class=\"overlay-launch\">\n    <img border=\"0\" src=\"https://cms.iopscience.org/7ebd1b32-0439-11e9-b401-cfe9679c40e3/iop-2016.png?guest=true\" alt=\"The Institute of Physics, find out more\">\n</a>\n<span class=\"overlay-set\">\n    <div class=\"tint-screen\"></div>\n    <div class=\"overlay-panel\">\n        <a title=\"Close\"  class=\"close-icon close-overlay\" tabindex=\"0\" role=\"button\" aria-describedby=\"close-icon-description\"><span class=\"icon-close\"></span></a>\n        <p id=\"close-icon-description\" class=\"offscreen-hidden\">Click here to close this overlay, or press the \"Escape\" key on your keyboard.</p>\n        <div class=\"overlay-img\">\n            <a href=\"\">\n                <img border=\"0\" src=\"https://cms.iopscience.org/7ebd1b32-0439-11e9-b401-cfe9679c40e3/iop-2016.png?guest=true\" alt=\"The Institute of Physics, find out more\">\n            </a>\n        </div>\n        <div class=\"overlay-text\">\n            <p>The Institute of Physics (IOP) is a leading scientific society promoting physics and bringing physicists together for the benefit of all. It has a worldwide membership of around 50 000 comprising physicists from all sectors, as well as those with an interest in physics. It works to advance physics research, application and education; and engages with policy makers and the public to develop awareness and understanding of physics. Its publishing company, IOP Publishing, is a world leader in professional scientific communications.</p> <p><a href=\"https://www.iop.org\">https://www.iop.org</a></p></div>\n        <p class=\"ta-c <span class=\"icon-newtab\">\n            </a></p>\n        </div>\n\n    <!-- End Email Alert -->\n<!-- End Email Alert --><!-- Start Citation Alert Link -->\n                        <p>\n<div class=\"jnl-notifications-wrapper\">\n    <a class=\"wd-jnl-email-alert\" href=\"https://myiopscience.iop.org/signin?origin=a0&return=https%3A%2F%2Fiopscience.iop.org%2Fmyiopscience%2Falerts%2Fsubscribe%3FarticleID%3D0004-637X%2F838%2F2%2F137\"><span\n            class=\"icon-alarm icon-alarm--jhp\"></span>Create citation alert</a>\n</div><!-- End Citation Alert Link -->\n                    </div>\n\t\t</div>\n    </div>\n    <!-- Article information ends -->\n<!-- Start Info top-->\n    <!-- end Info top --><div class=\"article-content\">\n\t<span id=\"articleId\" class=\"hide\">0004-637X/838/2/137</span>\n<!-- Start Abstract -->\n    <h2 id=\"artAbst\" class=\"collapse-blocked\">Abstract</h2>\n        <!-- Start article video abstract -->\n\t<!-- End article video abstract -->\n\t<div class=\"article-text wd-jnl-art-abstract cf\" itemprop=\"description\">\n            <p>We directly detect dust emission in an optically detected, multiply imaged galaxy lensed by the Frontier Fields cluster MACSJ0717.5+3745. We detect two images of the same galaxy at 1.1 mm with the AzTEC camera on the Large Millimeter Telescope leaving no ambiguity in the counterpart identification. This galaxy, MACS0717_Az9, is at <i>z</i>\u00a0&gt;\u00a04 and the strong lensing model (<i>\u03bc</i> = 7.5) allows us to calculate an intrinsic IR luminosity of 9.7\u00a0<b>&#x00d7;</b>\u00a010<sup>10</sup> <i>L</i><sub>\u2299</sub> and an obscured star formation rate of 14.6\u00a0\u00b1\u00a04.5 <i>M</i><sub>\u2299</sub> yr<sup>\u22121</sup>. The unobscured star formation rate from the UV is only 4.1\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.3 <i>M</i><sub>\u2299</sub> yr<sup>\u22121</sup>, which means the total star formation rate (18.7 \u00b1 4.5 <i>M</i><sub>\u2299</sub> yr<sup>\u22121</sup>) is dominated (75%\u201380%) by the obscured component. With an intrinsic stellar mass of only 6.9\u00a0<b>&#x00d7;</b>\u00a010<sup>9</sup> <i>M</i><sub>\u2299</sub>, MACS0717_Az9 is one of only a handful of <i>z</i>\u00a0&gt;\u00a04 galaxies at these lower masses that is detected in dust emission. This galaxy lies close to the estimated star formation sequence at this epoch. However, it does not lie on the dust obscuration relation (IRX-<i>\u03b2</i>) for local starburst galaxies and is instead consistent with the Small Magellanic Cloud attenuation law. This remarkable lower mass galaxy, showing signs of both low metallicity and high dust content, may challenge our picture of dust production in the early universe.</p></div>\n    <!-- End abstract class=\"linked-articles__btn event_read-more-articles\" data-event-action=\"Next Article\"><b>Next</b> article in issue<span\n\t\t\t\t\tclass=\"fa-icon fa-icon--right\"><svg aria-hidden=\"true\" class=\"reveal-container reveal-closed reveal-plus-icon bdt-1 mt-2 mb-2 wd-jnl-art-article-aas-related-links\">\n  <div class=\"replica-h3 mt-0\">\n    <a href=\"#\" class=\"reveal-trigger\" href=\"/journal/0004-637X/page/About%20Related%20Links\" target=\"_blank\">About Related Links</a></li>\n      \t</ul>\n    </div>\n  </div>\n</div>\n<!-- Start info bottom -->\n    <!-- End info bottom -->\n<!-- Start article full text -->\n\t<div xmlns:book=\"http://api.iop.org/Book/1.0/\" itemprop=\"articleBody\" class=\"wd-jnl-art-full-text article-text\">\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjaa6573s1\" name=\"apjaa6573s1\">1.\u00a0Introduction</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>Over the past 20 years, surveys at rest-frame UV wavelengths have mapped out the history of unobscured star formation from the present day back to <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a08 (Madau &amp; Dickinson <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib34\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib34\">2014</a>). However, the roughly equal brightness of the cosmic infrared and optical backgrounds informs us that half the light from the formation and evolution of galaxies is obscured by dust (Lagache et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib31\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib31\">2005</a>). Surveys with the <em>Spitzer Space Telescope</em> and the <em>Herschel Space Observatory</em> showed that the contribution from infrared-luminous galaxies to the star formation rate density increases dramatically from <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a00\u20132 (e.g., Caputi et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib11\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib11\">2007</a>; Murphy et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib37\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib37\">2011a</a>; Magnelli et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib35\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib35\">2013</a>). Beyond <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a03, our census of the dust-obscured, and hence <em>total</em>, star formation activity is severely incomplete.</p><p>Until recently, surveys of dust-obscured activity at <em>z</em>\u00a0&gt;\u00a03 detected only the bright ultra-luminous infrared galaxies (ULIRGs, <em>L</em><sub>IR</sub> &gt; 10<sup>12</sup> <em>L</em><sub>\u2299</sub>, Casey et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib12\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib12\">2014</a>). While ULIRGs are prevalent at high redshift and many are not extreme starbursts like their local counterparts, they are not responsible for creating the bulk of the stars in the universe (Lagache et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib31\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib31\">2005</a>). At <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a02, much of the cosmic star formation activity is occurring in galaxies with <em>L</em><sub>IR</sub>\u00a0&lt;\u00a010<sup>12</sup> <em>L</em><sub>\u2299</sub> (Murphy et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib37\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib37\">2011a</a>; Magnelli et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib35\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib35\">2013</a>). While these normal<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjaa6573fn1\">18</a></sup>\n galaxies can be selected at UV wavelengths, we have yet to directly detect most of their star formation activity as it is obscured by dust. The UV slope can provide an estimate of the dust extinction in the local universe (Meurer et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib36\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib36\">1999</a>); however, this correction is uncertain at high redshift, where star formation is clumpy (Guo et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib18\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib18\">2015</a>) and gas and dust are more widely distributed across the galaxy (e.g., Ivison et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib23\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib23\">2011</a>).</p><p>With its exceptional sensitivity, ALMA can directly detect dust in normal galaxies out to and beyond <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c\u00a03. In ALMA Cycles 0\u20132, several programs have pushed below the ULIRG limit, detecting dust in half a dozen UV-selected galaxies from <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a04\u20137.5 (e.g., Capak et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib10\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib10\">2015</a>; Watson et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib59\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib59\">2015</a>; Willott et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib60\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib60\">2015</a>; Dunlop et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib16\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib16\">2017</a>). These studies show mixed results, with some sources having significant dust emission while others remain undetected (e.g., Schaerer et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib48\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib48\">2015</a>; Bouwens et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib3\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib3\">2016</a>).</p><p>A complementary facility for directly detecting dust in <em>z</em>\u00a0&gt;\u00a04 galaxies is the Large Millimeter Telescope Alfonso Serrano (LMT, Hughes et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib21\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib21\">2010</a>). With a large aperture and fast mapping capability, the AzTEC camera (Wilson et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib61\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib61\">2008</a>) on the 32 m LMT can survey dust in galaxies down to <em>L</em><sub>IR</sub>\u00a0\u223c\u00a06\u00a0<b>&#x00d7;</b>\u00a010<sup>11</sup> <em>L</em><sub>\u2299</sub> regardless of redshift due to the negative <em>K</em>-correction. Gravitational lensing can be used to push even deeper. In this paper, we present the direct detection of dust in a multiply imaged normal galaxy at <em>z</em>\u00a0&gt;\u00a04 with AzTEC on LMT.</p><p>Throughout this paper we assume a cosmology with <em>H</em><sub>0</sub>\u00a0=\u00a070 km s<sup>\u22121</sup> Mpc<sup>\u22121</sup>, \u03a9<sub>M</sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.3, and \u03a9<sub>\u039b</sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.7.</p></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjaa6573s2\" name=\"apjaa6573s2\">2.\u00a0Data</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><h3 id=\"apjaa6573s2-1\" name=\"apjaa6573s2-1\">2.1.\u00a0Frontier Fields (FFs) Program</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>The FFs program<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjaa6573fn2\">19</a></sup>\n started as a large <em>Hubble Space Telescope</em> (<em>HST</em>) survey of low redshift clusters in order to identify and study high-redshift background galaxies that are gravitationally lensed. In this paper, we use the 13-band <em>HST</em> data, the <em>Spitzer</em>-IRAC imaging from 3.6 to 8 <em>\u03bc</em>m, and <em>K</em>-band imaging from Keck-MOSFIRE (program N097M and N135M, PI: Marchesini, Brammer et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib5\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib5\">2016</a>). The <em>HST</em> data include the F435W, F606W, F814W, F105W, F125W, F140W, and F160W images from the FF program; the F475W, F625W, F775W, and F850LP images from CLASH (Postman et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib43\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib43\">2012</a>); and the F275W and F336W images from the program GO-13389 (PI: Siana). The v2.1 UV-to-IRAC multi-wavelength photometric catalog used in this paper was constructed following Skelton et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib53\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib53\">2014</a>). The final catalog construction accounting for the intra-cluster light and contamination from brightest cluster galaxies will be described in H. Shipley et al. (2017, in preparation)</p><p>Since our target is a multiply imaged, strongly lensed galaxy, interpretation of its intrinsic properties will depend on the lensing model. STScI has released magnification maps as a function of background galaxy redshift for all FF clusters calculated from several independent lensing models.<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjaa6573fn3\">20</a></sup>\n In this paper, we use the updated lensing models from Limousin et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib33\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib33\">2016</a>) and Diego et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib15\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib15\">2015</a>), and we verified that our results are robust with other lensing models from STScI (Johnson et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib24\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib24\">2014</a>; Zitrin et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib63\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib63\">2015</a>). We present our results for two different lensing models to give a sense of how the parameters we are interested in (stellar mass, star formation rate, UV slope) change under different lensing models.</p></div><h3 id=\"apjaa6573s2-2\" name=\"apjaa6573s2-2\">2.2.\u00a0New AzTEC/LMT Observations</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>In 2014 November and December, we imaged the FF cluster MACSJ0717.5+3745 with AzTEC during early science with the LMT. During early science operations, we used the inner 32 m of the eventual 50 m aperture.<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjaa6573fn4\">21</a></sup>\n AzTEC is a 1.1 mm bolometer array camera, with a beam size of 8.5 arcsec (FWHM) on the 32 m LMT. Data were taken in good weather conditions (<em>\u03c4</em><sub>225 GHz</sub> = 0.05\u20130.12). The on-source integration time was 21.1 hr. Our map covers 25 sq.\u00a0arcmin field reaching a mean rms of 0.24 mJy (central rms is 0.19 mJy).</p><p>The calibration and analysis of the AzTEC data follow the procedure described in Wilson et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib61\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib61\">2008</a>) and Scott et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib50\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib50\">2008</a>). The results on the number counts and source properties from the full LMT FF program<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjaa6573fn5\">22</a></sup>\n will be presented in future papers. Here we focus on a unique and rare source detected in our AzTEC map (MACS0717_Az9), which is coincident with an optically detected, multiply imaged lensed galaxy (known as 5.1/5.2/5.3, Zitrin et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib62\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib62\">2009</a>). This is the only strongly lensed, multiply imaged system detected in our AzTEC survey. Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaa6573f1\">1</a> left shows AzTEC contours on the <em>HST</em> F160W image; two optical images (labeled 5.2 and 5.1) of the known multiply imaged system are detected with AzTEC (3.7 and 3.3<em>\u03c3</em> respectively). In Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaa6573s3-1\">3.1</a>, we demonstrate that at least half the millimeter flux detected by AzTEC must be associated with this system. A third &gt;3<em>\u03c3</em> AzTEC detection is visible in the top left corner of the left side of Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaa6573f1\">1</a>, but it is unassociated with the multiply imaged system that is the focus of this paper.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjaa6573f1\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjaa6573f1\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/838/2/137/1/apjaa6573f1_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636843505&amp;Signature=lhxlRsga%2BR6eLtHv5s13qxlOm7M%3D\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 1.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 1.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/838/2/137/1/apjaa6573f1_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636843505&amp;Signature=lhxlRsga%2BR6eLtHv5s13qxlOm7M%3D\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 1.</strong>\u00a0<em>HST</em> F160W image toward MACSJ0717 with AzTEC/LMT contours (3 and 3.5<em>\u03c3</em>) in red. Our AzTEC map covers a wider region than shown here. The 3<em>\u03c3</em> detection in the top left is unrelated to the multiply imaged galaxy. We show the two multiply imaged systems: 5.1/5.2/5.3 at <em>z</em>\u00a0&gt;\u00a04 (blue circles) and 12.1/12.2/12.3 at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.71 (green squares). The right panel shows a zoom-in of the millimeter detection MACS0717_Az9, which is at the bottom right of the left panel. The size of the image is roughly equal to the FWHM of the beam.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjaa6573f1\" href=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/838/2/137/1/apjaa6573f1_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636843505&amp;Signature=lhxlRsga%2BR6eLtHv5s13qxlOm7M%3D\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjaa6573f1\" href=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/838/2/137/1/apjaa6573f1_hr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636843505&amp;Signature=lwPqTvfa70x711XvF2zUU6U6aec%3D\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure></div><h3 id=\"apjaa6573s2-3\" name=\"apjaa6573s2-3\">2.3.\u00a0Robustness of Millimeter Detections</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>In order to test the robustness of MACS0717_Az9 both as a millimeter source and as the counterpart to the <em>z</em>\u00a0&gt;\u00a04 multiply imaged galaxy, we perform several simulations. We stress that since we have prior information on the positions of a known multiply imaged galaxy, we have more confidence in lower signal-to-noise detections.</p><p>First we determine the chance that our millimeter detections (3.7 and 3.3<em>\u03c3</em>) of the multiple-images 5.2 and 5.1 are spurious. We perform source extraction on 3000 noise maps. As with our original source list, we limit source extraction to regions of the map with noise &lt;0.4 mJy. We detect an average of 1 and 4 random &gt;3.7<em>\u03c3</em> and &gt;3.3<em>\u03c3</em> sources, respectively, in the noise maps. However, the sources we are interested in are not at random positions and specifically we detect two components of a previously known multiply imaged system. With this prior information, we find the chance of randomly detecting a\u00a0&gt;\u00a03.7<em>\u03c3</em> source within 1 AzTEC beam of 5.2 and a\u00a0&gt;\u00a03<em>\u03c3</em> source within 1 AzTEC beam of 5.1 is &lt;0.03%. We find the same answer if we vary the position of 5.2 and 5.1 on the map but conserve their relative separation. Therefore, the probability that our millimeter detection of this multiply imaged system (5.1 and 5.2) is a spurious detection is negligible.</p><p>Second, we test the chance that we should detect a multiply imaged source given the known lensing models and a model for a background population of millimeter sources. We develop 500 simulated maps using the empirical galaxy evolution model of B\u00e9thermin et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib1\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib1\">2012</a>) for the input background millimeter galaxies and the lensing models of MACSJ0717 from the CATS group (Limousin et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib33\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib33\">2016</a>). Here we report results using the <em>cored</em> mass model, and verified that there are no measurable differences with the <em>non-cored</em> mass model. We randomly populate simulated maps with millimeter sources down to intrinsic (e.g., non-lensed) 1.1 mm fluxes of \u22650.01 mJy. Redshifts are assigned to each millimeter source from the B\u00e9thermin et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib1\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib1\">2012</a>) model. Then we run the background population through the cluster using the mass model in LENSTOOL (Kneib et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib27\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib27\">1996</a>; Jullo et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib25\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib25\">2007</a>) to find the observed population of millimeter sources and ask how often the millimeter sources are multiply imaged. With no observed flux limit, multiple-image systems are found in all (99.4%) of our simulated maps, with an average of 6\u20137 systems per map. When we impose an observed flux limit of 0.7 mJy (i.e., &gt;3.5<em>\u03c3</em>), we find that 30% of these multiple systems have at least one image detectable in our simulated maps. Coupled with our estimated completeness limit of 50% at this low flux level (A. Monta\u00f1a et al. 2017, in preparation), our simulations predict that we will detect one multiply imaged system in our AzTEC map of MACS0717. Besides MACS0717_Az9, there are no other known multiply imaged sources in MACS0717 (using catalogs of known multiply imaged systems, e.g., Limousin et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib33\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib33\">2016</a>) that are individually detected in our AzTEC maps. We take the full list of multiply imaged sources including their magnification values and we stack the intrinsic millimeter flux for each multiply imaged source. We do not find that any other systems are detected, even when averaging the individual components in this way. Furthermore, none of the other AzTEC detections are in regions of strong magnification. Therefore, our simulations predict that we should detect one multiply imaged system like MACS0717_Az9.</p><p>Finally, we can further test the robustness of this millimeter detection by showing that the millimeter fluxes that we measure for 5.1, 5.2, and 5.3 are consistent with each other given their known magnifications (see Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaa6573s3-1\">3.1</a>). The results of all three of these simulations and tests show that we have unambiguously detected dust emission in this multiply imaged system.</p></div></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjaa6573s3\" name=\"apjaa6573s3\">3.\u00a0Analysis</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><h3 id=\"apjaa6573s3-1\" name=\"apjaa6573s3-1\">3.1.\u00a0Counterpart of MACS0717_Az9</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>Before we can discuss the nature of this millimeter source, we need to demonstrate that the multiply imaged system is the correct optical counterpart. From our simulations (A. Monta\u00f1a et al. 2017, in preparation), we find a positional accuracy for this system of 3.1 arcsec with 90% confidence. Within the search radius of MACS0717_Az9, we find two multiply imaged systems (Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaa6573f1\">1</a> right): 5.2 (<em>z</em> &gt; 4) and 12.2 (<em>z</em> = 1.71). But our AzTEC map also covers the other multiple images of these systems: 5.1/5.3 and 12.1/12.3 (Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaa6573f1\">1</a> left). We detect 5.1 in our AzTEC map at 3.3<em>\u03c3</em>. Source 5.3 has a lower magnification; as a result, the measured AzTEC flux is only 1.4<em>\u03c3</em> (Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjaa6573t1\">1</a>). Both 12.1 and 12.3 are undetected in our AzTEC map. In this Section, we show that the counterpart to MACS0717_Az9 must be 5.2.</p><div tabindex=\"-1\" id=\"apjaa6573t1\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\"><p><b>Table char=\"\u00b1\">0.119\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.032</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\">11.9\u00a0\u00b1\u00a03.8</td>\n</tr>\n</tbody></table><p><small>\n<p><strong>Notes.</strong></p>\n<a name=\"apjaa6573t1fna\" id=\"apjaa6573t1fna\"></a><sup> a</sup>From the Limousin et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib33\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib33\">2016</a>) non-cored lensing model (<em>z</em> = 4.1) and the Diego et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib15\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib15\">2015</a>) lensing model (<em>z</em> = 4.3). For corresponding magnifications,see Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjaa6573t2\">2</a>.\n<a name=\"apjaa6573t1fnb\" id=\"apjaa6573t1fnb\"></a><sup> b</sup>We measure the 1.1 mm flux at the known optical position of each multiple image to mitigate the effects of flux boosting.\n<a name=\"apjaa6573t1fnc\" id=\"apjaa6573t1fnc\"></a><sup> c</sup>Errors include the uncertainty due to the magnification and the photometric uncertainty.\n<a name=\"apjaa6573t1fnd\" id=\"apjaa6573t1fnd\"></a><sup> d</sup>Errors include the uncertainty due to the SED template (27%, Kirkpatrick et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib26\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib26\">2015</a>), the magnification and the photometric uncertainty.\n</small></p><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n\t\t\tDownload table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/0004-637X/838/2/137/suppdata/apjaa6573t1_ascii.txt?doi=10.3847/1538-4357/aa6573\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/838/2/137/1/apjaa6573t1_lr.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636843505&amp;Signature=jND%2F5f7PeXPCtSkHVult67XUZOc%3D\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div><p>The magnifications (<em>\u03bc</em>) are known for all components of systems 5 and 12 (Diego et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib15\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib15\">2015</a>; Limousin et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib33\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib33\">2016</a>), and so we test if the observed fluxes of each component are consistent with the predicted fluxes. Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaa6573f2\">2</a> left shows the observed fluxes of all three images of system 5 as the solid circles. If we assign some fraction <em>F</em> of the MACS0717_Az9 flux to 5.2 (<em>S</em><sub>5.2,obs</sub> = <em>S</em><sub>Az9</sub>\u2217<em>F</em>) and the remainder of the flux to 12.2, then we can predict the flux of 5.1 and 5.3 as follows:</p><div xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"display-eqn\" id=\"apjaa6573eqn1\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/838/2/137/1/apjaa6573eqn1.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636843505&amp;Signature=Ag9zLTiZLhN32jYd5eIGmvqxuMQ%3D\" alt=\"Equation (1)\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex; mode=display\">\\begin{eqnarray}&&{S}_{5.1,\\mathrm{pred}}=({S}_{5.2,\\mathrm{obs}}/{\\mu }_{5.2})\\times {\\mu }_{5.1},\\end{eqnarray}\n\t\t\t\t\\tag{\n\t\t\t\t1\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t</script></span></div><p>\n</p><div xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"display-eqn\" id=\"apjaa6573eqn2\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/838/2/137/1/apjaa6573eqn2.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636843505&amp;Signature=eLdZxJ7ucq3%2F%2BcPCbjsQbv5LoWQ%3D\" alt=\"Equation (2)\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex; mode=display\">\\begin{eqnarray}&&{S}_{5.3,\\mathrm{pred}}=({S}_{5.2,\\mathrm{obs}}/{\\mu }_{5.2})\\times {\\mu }_{5.3}\\end{eqnarray}\n\t\t\t\t\\tag{\n\t\t\t\t2\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t</script></span></div><p>where <em>\u03bc</em><sub>5.2</sub>, <em>\u03bc</em><sub>5.1</sub>, and <em>\u03bc</em><sub>5.3</sub> denote the known magnifications of 5.2, 5.1, and 5.3. The triangles and squares in the left panel of Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaa6573f2\">2</a> show the predicted fluxes from two different lensing models assuming <em>F</em>\u00a0=\u00a01, which are remarkably consistent with the observed fluxes of 5.1 and 5.3. If instead we perform this calculation assuming the millimeter emission comes from 12.2 (Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaa6573f2\">2</a> right), we find that the observed fluxes of 12.1 and 12.3 are inconsistent with the expected fluxes under each of the two lensing models.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjaa6573f2\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjaa6573f2\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/838/2/137/1/apjaa6573f2_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636843505&amp;Signature=GPED2rbuaOXgLTHjlkwLLRs86f8%3D\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 2.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 2.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/838/2/137/1/apjaa6573f2_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636843505&amp;Signature=GPED2rbuaOXgLTHjlkwLLRs86f8%3D\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 2.</strong>\u00a0Demonstration that MACS0717_Az9 is most likely associated with the multiply imaged galaxy 5.2. (Left) Red circles show the observed 1.1 mm fluxes of the three multiply imaged components, 5.1, 5.2, and 5.3, from our AzTEC maps. The dark blue triangles and light blue squares show the predicted millimeter fluxes of 5.1 and 5.3 assuming that MACS0717_Az9 is associated with 5.2 and applying the known lensing magnifications (Table <a class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjaa6573t2\">2</a>) from the Limousin et al. (<a class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib33\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib33\">2016</a>) and Diego et al. (<a class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib15\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib15\">2015</a>) lensing models, respectively. The error bars on the blue points include the photometric uncertainty and the magnification uncertainty. (Right) Same as the left panel but for the multiply imaged source 12.1/12.2/12.3 showing the observed fluxes are inconsistent with the predicted fluxes under these two different lensing models.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjaa6573f2\" href=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/838/2/137/1/apjaa6573f2_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636843505&amp;Signature=GPED2rbuaOXgLTHjlkwLLRs86f8%3D\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjaa6573f2\" href=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/838/2/137/1/apjaa6573f2_hr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636843505&amp;Signature=CUfYIaRef%2BbgWeAf5Qv%2FhjCRFs0%3D\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><p>Next, we calculate the <em>P</em>-value for all values of <em>F</em> from 0 to 1 under the hypothesis that the predicted fluxes equal the observed fluxes:</p><div xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"display-eqn\" id=\"apjaa6573eqn3\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/838/2/137/1/apjaa6573eqn3.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636843505&amp;Signature=Js4RA5CbJSozqm72wcuoxJyaIxA%3D\" alt=\"Equation (3)\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex; mode=display\">\\begin{eqnarray}&&{S}_{5.1,\\mathrm{obs}}-{S}_{5.1,\\mathrm{pred}}\\sim N(0,{\\sigma }_{5.1,\\mathrm{obs}}^{2}+{\\sigma }_{5.1,\\mathrm{pred}}^{2}),\\end{eqnarray}\n\t\t\t\t\\tag{\n\t\t\t\t3\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t</script></span></div><p>\n</p><div xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"display-eqn\" id=\"apjaa6573eqn4\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/838/2/137/1/apjaa6573eqn4.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636843505&amp;Signature=8GbcfBYjQ0bNFlYku%2BfbunAN2bw%3D\" alt=\"Equation (4)\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex; mode=display\">\\begin{eqnarray}&&{S}_{5.3,\\mathrm{obs}}-{S}_{5.3,\\mathrm{pred}}\\sim N(0,{\\sigma }_{5.3,\\mathrm{obs}}^{2}+{\\sigma }_{5.3,\\mathrm{pred}}^{2})\\end{eqnarray}\n\t\t\t\t\\tag{\n\t\t\t\t4\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t</script></span></div><p>where <em>N</em> is a normal distribution. <em>\u03c3</em><sub>5.1,pred</sub> and <em>\u03c3</em><sub>5.3,pred</sub> include the uncertainties from all quantities in Equations (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"eqnref\" href=\"#apjaa6573eqn1\">1</a>) and (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"eqnref\" href=\"#apjaa6573eqn2\">2</a>): the flux measurement of 5.2, the magnification of 5.2, and the magnification of 5.1 and 5.3, respectively. We perform this hypothesis test for 5.1, 5.3, 12.1, and 12.3, and combine the <em>P</em>-values using Fisher's method (Fisher <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib17\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib17\">1925</a>). The combined <em>P</em>-value as a function of <em>F</em> is plotted in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaa6573f3\">3</a>. We can reject the null hypothesis that <em>F</em>\u00a0\u2264\u00a00.45 at a significance level of 0.05; this means that at least half the flux of MACS0717_Az9 <em>must</em> be associated with 5.2. For the analysis in this paper we assume the most likely scenario: that all of the flux of MACS0717_Az9 is associated with 5.2 (i.e., <em>F</em> = 1). In Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaa6573s4-3\">4.3</a>, we discuss how our main results are affected under the conservative assumption that only half the millimeter flux is associated with 5.2.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjaa6573f3\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjaa6573f3\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/838/2/137/1/apjaa6573f3_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636843505&amp;Signature=XliMxlq6EsEb3XTGuq9jprDMlHI%3D\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 3.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 3.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.68.1/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/838/2/137/1/apjaa6573f3_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636843505&amp;Signature=XliMxlq6EsEb3XTGuq9jprDMlHI%3D\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 3.</strong>\u00a0<em>P</em>-value from testing the hypothesis that the observed fluxes of 5.1/5.3 and 12.1/12.3 are consistent with the predicted fluxes as a function of the fraction of the flux from MACS0717_Az9 that is attributed to 5.2. The most likely scenario is that all of the flux from MACS0717_Az9 is associated with 5.2, and we can rule out the scenario where \u226445% of the millimeter flux is coming from 5.2.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjaa6573f3\" href=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/838/2/137/1/apjaa6573f3_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636843505&amp;Signature=XliMxlq6EsEb3XTGuq9jprDMlHI%3D\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjaa6573f3\" href=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/838/2/137/1/apjaa6573f3_hr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636843505&amp;Signature=YQl6JkWduq7JFc%2FnakE2WUdsSsM%3D\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure></div><h3 id=\"apjaa6573s3-2\" name=\"apjaa6573s3-2\">3.2.\u00a0Redshift</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>The multiple images (5.1, 5.2, 5.3) have independent redshift estimates from blind photometric redshift catalogs (Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaa6573f4\">4</a> right, see also Postman et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib43\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib43\">2012</a>) and from the lensing models (Diego et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib15\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib15\">2015</a>; Limousin et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib33\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib33\">2016</a>, see also Johnson et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib24\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib24\">2014</a>; Zitrin et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib63\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib63\">2015</a>). Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjaa6573t2\">2</a> summarizes the redshift estimates for each multiple image. As described in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaa6573s3-3\">3.3</a>, fitting the optical spectral energy distribution gives photometric redshifts of \u223c4.4\u20134.6. The lensing models agree on a redshift of <em>z</em>\u00a0\u2273\u00a04 for this multiply imaged source, and are consistent with the \u00b13<em>\u03c3</em> limits from the photometric redshift. Treu et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib58\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib58\">2015</a>) suggest a low redshift solution of <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a00.928 for image 5.1 based on <em>HST</em> grism data. However, we do not see any strong features in the spectrum and this redshift is not compatible with the mass models of MACSJ0717.5+3745.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjaa6573f4\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjaa6573f4\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/838/2/137/1/apjaa6573f4_lr.jpg?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636843505&amp;Signature=A5ACWSITsoYm%2FLZvbPN%2BVEcs5u8%3D\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 4.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; id=\"apjaa6573t2fnb\"></a><sup> b</sup>Uncertainties on the redshift are not provided for this lensing model.\n</small></p><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n\t\t\tDownload table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/0004-637X/838/2/137/suppdata/apjaa6573t2_ascii.txt?doi=10.3847/1538-4357/aa6573\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"https://cfn-live-content-bucket-iop-org.s3.amazonaws.com/journals/0004-637X/838/2/137/1/apjaa6573t2_lr.gif?AWSAccessKeyId=AKIAYDKQL6LTV7YY2HIK&amp;Expires=1636843505&amp;Signature=jcuhwm9WLdTqqE5OLz%2FuZ09h5ow%3D\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div><p>In this paper, we consider two redshift solutions: (1) <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a04.1\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.2 from the non-cored mass model of Limousin et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib33\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib33\">2016</a>), and (2) <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a04.3 from the lens model of Diego et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib15\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib15\">2015</a>). Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjaa6573t2\">2</a> lists the magnifications for each of these solutions. While a spectroscopic redshift for this multiply imaged system will be important for further studies, the uncertainty in the analysis in this paper is less affected because of the negative <em>K</em>-correction, which makes the relation between millimeter flux and luminosity roughly constant between <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01\u20136.</p></div><h3 id=\"apjaa6573s3-3\" name=\"apjaa6573s3-3\">3.3.\u00a0UV to Near-IR Properties</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>Measuring the UV to near-IR photometry for this multiply imaged system is complicated since the images are extended (Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaa6573f1\">1</a> right) and resolve into separate entries in our multi-wavelength catalog. We take the weighted mean of these entries to estimate the total flux in each band for 5.1, 5.2, and 5.3. Having three lensed images of the same galaxy provides an independent check on the photometry.</p><p>We fit the de-magnified UV to the near-IR photometry using FAST (Kriek et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib29\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib29\">2009</a>) adopting Bruzual &amp; Charlot (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib7\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib7\">2003</a>) stellar populations (BC03), a Chabrier (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib13\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib13\">2003</a>) IMF and a delayed exponentially declining SFH in order to determine the stellar mass. Since we find that this galaxy lies closer to the Small Magellanic Cloud (SMC) dust curve (see Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaa6573s4-1\">4.1</a>), we perform the SED fitting using SMC dust attenuation and sub-solar metallicity<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjaa6573fn6\">23</a></sup>\n (<em>Z</em> = 0.2 <b>&#x00d7;</b> <em>Z</em><sub>\u2299</sub>). The difference in stellar mass between a Chabrier (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib13\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib13\">2003</a>) and Kroupa (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib30\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib30\">2001</a>) IMF is negligible (e.g., Speagle et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa6573bib54\" id=\"fnref-apjaa6573bib54\">2014</a>). The uncertainties in the stellar masses include the photometric error, the uncertainty in the magnification (including an additional 10% for differential lensing, Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaa6573s3-5\">3.5</a>), and the uncertainty in the SED fitting. The stellar masses and their 68% confidence ranges are given in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjaa6573t3\">3</a>. The left panel of Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaa6573f4\">4</a> shows the SED fits for the <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a04.1 lens model; given the large magnification values for each multiple image, the de-magnified SEDs show very good agreement.</p><div tabindex=\"-1\" id=\"apjaa6573t3\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\"><p><b>Table
